                           Purpose
To determine the short and longterm traffic impacts associated 
with the closure of Millwood Avenue to vehicular traffic between 
E. Jubal Early Drive and Apple Blossom Drive and provide for:
     · Alternate vehicular access locations to Shenandoah 
       University
     · Improvements necessary to address the impacts of the 
       street closure
               l
     · Improved pedestrian and bicycle attractiveness/viability 
       to and thru the University

Potential Measures of Effectiveness (MOEs)
·   Vehicle delay at intersections 
·   Corridor travel times (autos & transit vehicles)
·   Potential changes to transit routes, lengths and stop location 
·   Average wait time for a `walk' signal at a crosswalk 
·   Travel times for pedestrian
·   Perceived quality of walking routes
·   Perceived quality of bicycling routes
·   Conflict diagrams for all high accident locations
·   Qualitative analyses (sight lines, speeds, hierarchy transition, 
    campus access, wayfinding)

From: Mike Steadman [mailto:MikeS@susqtech.com]
Sent: Monday, September 20, 2010 5:10 PM
To: Careers@gsatrans.com
Subject: Winchester, VA - Millwood Traffic Diversion Study citizen comments
 
To whom it may concern:   
 
Kindly please forward this email to the lead consultant managing the Winchester, VA ­ Millwood Ave. / Jubal Early Drive 
traffic diversion study.  
 
Unfortunately, I am unable to attend tonight's citizen meeting where I believe a member of your team is presenting on 
this subject. 
 
I own a 65person technology consulting firm headquartered in downtown Winchester, VA.  On a daily basis  about 25% 
of my staff uses the section of road being studied (myself included ­ I live in nearby Stephens City, and exit I81 each 
morning between 8:30 and 9AM). 
 
Regarding your recommendation  I can personally submit as evidence, the following information: 
 
     ·         This section of road is frequently under discussion among those of us who use it every day  I've seen a few 
              (remnants of) accidents that have occurred at the entrance to this section of road  and I have personally 
              witnessed (guessing) 10+ nearmisses over the past few years of traveling this section of road.  For those who 
              don't know this intersection ­ it is obviously very confusing. 
     ·         Before the "no right turn on red" was installed for vehicles exiting I81 from the North ­ I have had to quickly 
              veer left and `stay straight' on multiple occasions ­ due to traffic coming off of I81 (at a very high rate of speed) 
              ­ recent traffic signal adjustments have helped ­ but many people still ignore the `no right on red' and take the 
              right anyway, creating a mergesituation. 
     ·         For me ­ and for a few folks who work with me ­ staying straight and turning at the right is not a big deal or 
              inconvenience  it probably won't add more than a few seconds to the daily trip, and I won't be worried about 
              hitting a student or dealing with crazy merger issues anymore.  It just makes sense. 
     ·         There is clearly a problem with the current traffic pattern, noone could argue this.  But to what extent ­ well 
              that's where you (and citizens like me) come in.  My opinion is simple  because Shenandoah University does 
              quite a bit for the city of Winchester ­ if this helps the University, and simultaneously makes the roads in 
              Winchester safer ­ it seems like a nobrainer.   
 
Therefore  I'm in full support of making this change ­ eliminating the road altogether, and directing all westbound Rt. 
50 / Jubal Early traffic to the existing intersection / righthand turn. 
 
                                                                 1
I'm happy to provide further info/comments upon request. 
 
Thanks for your time. 
 
Michael L. Steadman 
President, SusQtech

From: Steve Wisecarver [mailto:lfwises@comcast.net]
Sent: Saturday, September 18, 2010 4:43 PM
To: kltaylor@shentel.net
Subject: Millwood Avenue

My wife and I use the section of Milwood Avenue that Shenandoah University wants to close several times each week. It
is a quick and convenient way to avoid the congested roads in the Apple Blossom Mall/ Pleasant Valley Rd. area. If SU is
allowed to close it, hundreds of motorists will be inconvenienced, traffic will increase as will road rage and accidents,
commuting time will be longer, and shoppers may be less likely to patronize businesses in that area. Traffic will increase
on the route to Winchester Medical Center, possibly hindering ambulances en route with critically ill patients. If the
university really believes that the road is a safety hazard to its students, it should construct an elevated walkway for them
at its own expense.
Stephen E. Wisecarver
Karen S. Wisecarver
102 N. Greenway Ave.
Boyce, VA 22620

Subject: Millwood closing

I am against closing of Millwood Ave. Reasons: congestion added to Jubal Early. Biking more dangerous on
Jubal Early. More complex and increased time to get into town. More ozone creation. Intersections on Jubal
Early don't clear now with cars stuck in intersections as lights change: adding more cars would create standstill
traffic. Downtown merchants would be hurt as people add up all the aggravations to going downtown such as
meters, 4-way stops, curb bumpouts, middle of road obstructions, low, low speed limits (25) and now fighting
Jubal Early and Pleasant Valley road.

L. Sullivan

Hello,
 We are residents of downtown Winchester and we recently have had many changes shoved down our throats.When they

signs.There is an incredible amount of traffic in the Rt 50,81, and 522 area and with all the cars that travel through that
area in a day it really makes no sense to divert half of that traffic onto overused roads and overloaded intersections.What
is the true purpose?The convenience of students crossing the road?Please dont sneak another traffic snarling on us.We
have taken alot of pointless change in the last year.It seems as though every time a "study " is done the deed is already a
done deal and we only have a day to protest.I hope people see the pointlessness of this road closure.It is very difficult to
travel from the north end of town to the south!Please reconsider.

Daniel B. VanPelt
From:                     Karen Taylor [kltaylor@shentel.net]

Subject:                  FW: Millwood MPO Study




From: jennybousquet@comcast.net [mailto:jennybousquet@comcast.net]
Sent: Monday, September 27, 2010 11:23 PM
To: cprice@shentel.net
Cc: kltaylor@shentel.net
Subject: Millwood MPO Study

       Dear Mr. Price:



Regarding the potential closure of Millwood Avenue in Winchester, I find the need to put my thoughts in a
letter rather than to only voice them through last week's public input session. I hope the session was productive,
but I didn't personally find it to be a fully satisfactory forum for calm, reasoned discussion and appreciation for
subtlety. I hope you will forward my comments to the consultants.



First, let me describe my position in the community in order to provide context for my comments. My husband
and I moved to the region in 1993 and have owned a home in Winchester's historic district since 1994. I've
worked full-time for various employers for all of my time in the community. I've raised two children who went
to public schools ­ the second one having graduated from Handley High School this year. For five years, I
worked in Strasburg, Virginia. Since 2000, I've worked in an administrative position at Shenandoah University.
My office is located downtown but I typically travel to campus from two to ten times weekly for meetings or
events. I also travel through the study area and along Millwood Avenue regularly for various other reasons.



More frequently than not, when traveling west into town, I take Millwood Avenue. I realize that I would have to
change that habit if a portion of Millwood were closed ­ as would all those people who spoke to that fact last
week. For me, the fact that a Millwood closure would require us to do something differently from the way we
now do it (or even that we find that route convenient) carries absolutely no weight in the decision about whether
to close a portion of the road. Likewise, any focus on the nostalgia that some people seem to feel about the way
things were 25 years ago ­ when the population of Winchester and Frederick County was 60% of what it is
today ­ does not illumine today's decision-making process.



I was especially interested to hear the many opinions (from those favoring as well as opposing road closure) that
people expressed about what they believed would make the focus area safer. I agree that safety needs to be of
paramount concern in whatever recommendations come out of the current study. While people's perspectives,
                                                         1
observations, suggestions, and "common sense" conclusions are worthy of consideration, it's very important to
me that all those be vetted against industry standards and tested for truthfulness by experts who have the
knowledge and skill necessary to do so. I sincerely hope that the consultants will do just that. The decision
about what to do about Millwood should not be a popularity contest. MPO members and elected leaders in the
community need to base their decisions on reasoned judgment, relevant data, and a responsibility to serve the
long-term interests of our entire community. They need to have courage of conviction and not simply act or
vote out of a desire to please noisy citizens on any side of the argument.



While safety cannot be compromised, I also agree with the consultants' proposed goals related to convenience,
aesthetics, and balance. Within those goals, I can envision various objectives and a great deal of overlap. For
instance, I think that reducing confusion with the creation of a clear and understandable roadway into the City is
important. In providing that, we would provide both convenience for newcomers or occasional visitors and
safety for general vehicular traffic. At the same time, this more coherent gateway to the city might provide a
better opportunity for aesthetics.

I do have some specific observations and ideas regarding this area of roadway based on my own experience
over the years:



    1. The "Y" as approached from the east/exit off the interstate is confusing to drivers unfamiliar
       with the area. There's a very short time for approaching drivers to take in all the possibilities,
       decide on the right course, and get into the correct lanes. Furthermore, they face impatience
       by local drivers who are eager to swerve into their desired lanes ­ creating the potential for
       collisions and resulting in many near-misses.

        Tourists, shoppers and travelers who have an initial bad impression about entering Winchester
        from Exit 313 will have a negative first impression and may not be inclined to make return
        visits.


    2. Even for drivers familiar with the area, the approach to the Y can be very hectic and potentially
       unsafe, especially when traffic is heavy and/or too swift, as it often is. If the recommendations
       coming out of this study can address ways to calm ­ but not clog ­ traffic, it would be a great
       benefit.


    3. I disagree with the gentleman at the input session who said he could tell visitors they could
       turn right off the interstate and just stay straight on Millwood into town. In fact, I find that I need
       to tell visitors to pay close attention in order to stay in the correct lane. At the intersection of
       Apple Blossom and Millwood, drivers on Millwood need to make an incredibly awkward and
       unsafe left merge in order to stay straight rather than finding themselves in a right-hand turn
       lane onto Pleasant Valley Avenue. Farther west down the road, they stay straight but find
       themselves on Gerrard Street ­ and later Handley Boulevard.


    4. During the time I worked in Strasburg and came home every evening off Exit 313, there were
       many times when there was poor visibility from heavy rain, fog, or snow, making it difficult or
       impossible to see lane markings. Even in moderate traffic, this made the section of Millwood
                                                        2
       with the awkward left merge feel totally chaotic ­ with cars coming from merging lanes and
       crossing among one another to go in the various directions.


    5. I've noticed that when discussion of accompanying bicyclists and pedestrians come up, many
       people jump to the conclusion that the issue is with SU students. Granted, with the close
       proximity to SU, student mobility needs to be considered. However, attention to
       cyclist/pedestrian needs goes far beyond students.

       In the early 2000s, Winchester City Council commissioned a broad, citizen-based study effort
       called Opportunity Winchester. It focused on ways to enhance Winchester as a place to live,
       work, and visit. Dozens of citizens must have given hundreds of hours of service to
       Opportunity Winchester through its various committees, and many more citizens contributed
       through various public input opportunities. Eventually, a number of recommendations came
       out of that study ­ with the development of pedestrian and bicycle pathways being at the very
       top of the list of desired enhancements.

       While it is true that relatively few people currently use Jubal Early as a pedestrian path or
       bikeway of choice, I believe that is to a large extent because we have made little effort to
       make the area safe, inviting, or even tolerant toward walkers and cyclists. As teenagers, my
       children used bicycles as a frequent mode of transportation through town. They and I wished
       that they could take their bikes safely to destinations such as the movie theatres and shopping
       centers ­ but the fact is that Winchester roads just weren't built with bicycle access in mind.
       Thankfully, the city is slowly (too slowly, in my opinion) becoming more bike-friendly and
       pedestrian-friendly. I hope that any reconfiguration of roads in the study area will substantially
       improve bicycle/pedestrian access. I hope it will help guide the progression of the Green Circle
       through the area and that it will take into consideration linkages with existing or planned
       bicycle trails eastward into the county.


I appreciate the MPO taking on the task of this study and I look forward to learning more from the consultants'
recommendations.



Sincerely,



Jennifer Bousquet

                           Purpose
To determine the short and longterm traffic impacts associated 
with the closure of Millwood Avenue to vehicular traffic between 
E. Jubal Early Drive and Apple Blossom Drive and provide for:
     · Alternate vehicular access locations to Shenandoah 
       University
     · Improvements necessary to address the impacts of the 
       street closure
               l
     · Improved pedestrian and bicycle attractiveness/viability 
       to and thru the University
Study Focus
                        Alternatives

1) No Build  Future Conditions Scenario 
      No improvements or access changes

2) Millwood Avenue Closure Scenario  
      Closure of Millwood Avenue from E. Jubal Early Drive to 
      Apple
          l  Blossom
              l       Drive
                      Policy Guidance

· WinFred Plan
   ­ Provide safe and efficient road system
   ­ Encourage growth by providing convenient parking and system of 
     sidewalks and walking paths
   ­ Encourage use of alternate modes of transportation
· Bike & Ped Plan
   ­ Bike and ped facilities serve a dual purpose of recreation and 
     transportation
   ­ Have convenient and safe option of traveling by foot and bicycle
     2010 Comp Plan Mobility Objectives

· Create and maintain a safe,, efficient,
                                        , and environmentally
                                                            y 
  sustainable transportation network that is interconnected, 
  multimodal, and that facilitates walkable urban lane use 
  patterns less dependent upon personal vehicle use

TECHNICAL MEMORANDUM 
 
    To:             Millwood Diversion Study  Transportation Advisory Committee

    From:           Daniel B. VanPelt, P.E., PTOE 
                    Robert B. Schiesel, P.E.                                                             

    Date:           March 28, 2011 
    Subject:        Millwood Avenue Traffic Diversion Study
                    Response to Comments 
 
This memorandum contains responses to comments received from TAC members on the Millwood Avenue Traffic Diversion 
Study  draft  report  dated  January  10,  2011.    Detailed  comments  were  received  from  Tim  Youmans  ­  City  of  Winchester 
Planning  via  email  dated  January  26,  2011  and  Terry  Short  ­  VDOT  Staunton  District  Planning  via  memorandum  dated 
January 28, 2011.  The following sections are formatted with each comment or groups of comments followed by a response 
in red text.  

City of Winchester Planning Comments, January 26, 2011 
p. v       change `Effusiveness' to `Effectiveness'  Word changed 
p. v       bullet at bottom of page notes that `reduce speeds' is an MOE used to evaluate the alternatives, but it does not 
appear as an MOE on the chart on p.25  The bullets on the bottom of the page are not MOEs, but instead list objectives 
related to the goals of the study 
p.vi       many of the bulleted MOE's listed here do not match up with the MOE's on the p.25 chart  The bullets are not 
MOEs, but instead list objectives related to the goals of the study 
p.vii       2nd bullet at top of page states "it increases convenience by reducing vehicular delay,..."  This statement is not 
backed up by the data.  The simulation supports a reduction in "overall" delay for the study area while it is true some 
movements do experience increased delay while others experience a reduction 
p. 4       typo `longrang(e)'  Text amended 
p. 8       last para: it appears from the data that Millwood Ave traffic accounts for 42% (not 44%) of the inbound AM Peak Hr 
traffic.  42% is the percentage of traffic that turns at all approaches at the Pleasant Valley/Jubal Early intersection on 
Figure 3.  Figures 4 and 5 contain the percentage of traffic using Millwood Avenue. 
p. 8       last para: "A similarly high number is seen in the reverse movement from downtown towards the West." Should the 
last word read "East" (not "West")?  Text amended 
p. 9       Suggest adding the word `Existing' or `2007' to the front of the titles of Figure 4 and 5.  "2007" added 
p. 9       Based upon the numbers provided in Figure 20 for Intersections # 7 & 8 on p. 38 it appears that the inbound traffic 
             flow during the AM Peak Hr totals 1,765 vehs with 740 taking Millwood and 1,025 vehs taking Jubal Early. If so, 
             then the percentages in Figure 4 should show a 42%/58% split.  The splits in Figure 4 were taken from the Synchro 
             files provided by the City.  The files provided contain more information than what is shown on Figure 20.  That 
             said, the AM Synchro files provided by the City were incorrect and the analysis has been updated. 
p. 9       Based upon the numbers provided in Figure 20 for Intersections # 7 & 8 on p. 38 it appears that the inbound traffic 
             flow during the PM Peak Hr totals 1,645 vehs with 645 taking Millwood and 1,000 vehs taking Jubal Early. If so, 
             then the percentages in Figure 5 should show a 39%/61% split. That seems to be a pretty significant difference 
             from the 32%/68% split that was presented at public mtgs. The splits in Figure 5 were taken from the Synchro files 
             provided by the City.  The files provided contain more information than what is shown on Figure 20.

p.25      The following comments pertain to the foldout MOE Matrix on this page: 
     For consistency, the titles of Alts across the top should note the new signal(s) when proposed. Alts 1b & 1c note 
            the new signal at Apple Blossom/Millwood. Alts 1e, 2, & 2a do not note the new signal. Alt 1d does not note the 2 
            new signals. Table amended 
     See comments above for inconsistency between MOEs on the Matrix vs. on pp. v & vi. The bullets on pp v & vi are 
            not MOEs, but instead list objectives related to the goals of the study 
     Under the last Safety MOE, the change in # of veh conflict points seems understated for many of the alts. Just the 
            removal of the strangely configured intersection of University & Millwood (Int#6) appears to eliminate between 16 
            and 25 conflict points. That certainly affects Alts 1c, 1d, 2, & 2a more positively than noted.   Table amended 
     For the 1st MOE pertaining to Convenience (Change in # of ints at/over capacity), is the timeframe shortterm or 
            longterm? Only shortterm traffic volumes were assumed in the selection of the alternative that was then tested 
            against existing conditions for longterm. 
     For the last MOE  pertaining to Convenience (Local Access), it seems like the Mall, SU, and `other businesses' 
            properly fit under the heading of `Local Access' (meaning within the study area), but Access to Downtown should 
            probably be listed separately.   Table amended to just say "Access" 
     Under the first Appearance MOE (Intuitiveness), I believe there is a change to the intuitiveness of all Alts except 1 
            & 1a. The reconfiguration of Intersections # 5 & 6 where certain through movements get changed to left or right 
            turn movements represents a change. For Alts 1d, 1e, 2, & 2a, the entries note that there is the same link to/from 
            downtown. However, for Alts 1d, 2, & 2a, the link to downtown is changed. For Alt 1e, the link from downtown is 
            greatly improved and for Alts 1c & 1d, the link from downtown is link is changed. The word "same" in this MOE 
            means that in the given alternative the same link is used to approach town as is used to depart, not the same 
            links as are used today for these patterns.  This comment seems to refer to change in familiarity rather than 
            intuitiveness of the system.  There would certainly be an adjustment for familiar users with most of these 
            alternatives. 
     Under the last Appearance MOE (Provision for gateway feature), there seems to be a bias in the evaluation--For 
            Alts 2 & 2a, the entry is `improved' while the entry for 1e (which also renders a single entry corridor) reads 
            `somewhat improved'. It would seem that based upon 1e having the long distance before a decision point (1,250') 
            it would have to be as good or better than Alts 2 & 2a which have slightly shorter decision point distances (1,150 

Gorove/Slade                                                                                               www.goroveslade.com

              each).  The curvature of the Jubal Early alignment would allow better sightlines to see an oncoming feature and

         For the 2nd Balance MOE (Local Access/Commuter Convenience), I think the net change in # of traffic signals 
              encountered on the inbound and outbound trips between I81 and the Pleasant Valley Rd/Millwood intersection 
              should be noted. Alts 1b, 1c, 2, & 2a each introduce 1 new signal both inbound and outbound. Alt 1d introduces 2

              at the next intersection (#5).  The westbound free flow right turn will be the predominant movement and the 
              analysis is showing no issue with the merge or weave.

p.55      For Intersection#5, it seems hard to believe that the AM & PM Peak Hr LOS for the eastbound approach is as good 
           as C/C if the 1000 or so freeflowing diverted northbound peak hr vehicles are only experiencing an average of 3.8 
           to 9 seconds of delay per the figures in Table 1 on page 34.  This result is based on the traffic models as described 
           in the report.  The signal cycle length assumed for the new traffic signal is short enough to allow for this type of 
           result.   
p. 60     2nd bullet at bottom of page: Again, the data does not substantiate that vehicle delays would be reduced with Alt 2a 
           as compared to the No Build.  The simulation supports a reduction in "overall" delay for the study area while it is 
           true some movements do experience increased delay while others experience a reduction. 

VDOT Staunton District Planning, January 28, 2011 
     1.   Many approaches in all models that have been developed using a negative lost time adjust.  We understand that 
          the City of Winchester provided the consultant Synchro v.6 base files and the consultant in turn converted these 
          files to Synchro v.7.  There is a known conversion bug between v.6 and v.7 which alters the lost time adjustments 
          to negative values while not changing allclear timings.  As a result, conditions may not be accurately depicted in 
          any of the models developed for the study.  This needs to be revised.  
          (http://trafficware.infopop.cc/eve/forums/a/tpc/f/1221051642/m/9361013284) 
          Analysis was revised with bug fixed and correct lost times. 
     2.   Many signals have the same cycle lengths and timing for both AM and PM conditions.  Directional volume 
          variations likely would require a change in timings and phasing's to reflect field conditions.  By not accounting for 
          peak hour directional changes, the models may not be reflecting future conditions, but more importantly existing 
          conditions, accurately.  We would suggest that the network offsets be optimized in the models at a minimum.  By 
          way of low cost example, we would suggest that the consultant run a SimTraffic animation of existing AM or PM 
          conditions and visually compare the operations to actual existing traffic conditions in the study area.  The incorrect 
          files for the AM Synchro were provided to Gorove/Slade.  The analysis was revised using the correct Synchro 
          files. 
     3.   Future signal timing is coded the same as the existing signal timing.  Volumes are predicted to increase by several 
          hundred vehicles for certain movements and approaches and yet future signal timings have not been modified to 
          adjust for these conditions.  Not doing so can portray deficiencies in some movements inaccurately.  We would 
          suggest that all models be optimized to the signal network that they are assigned to.  Please revise.  Analysis and 
          results updated.   
     4.   The existing traffic volumes do not seem realistic.  For example, the SBL at the Pleasant Valley/Jubal Valley 
          intersection is 50, and the SBL at Apple Blossom/Jubal Early is 500 for both AM and PM.  We question why a 
          motorist would choose a route where they would experience a longer delay to make a leftturn at Apple 
          Blossom/Jubal Early.  The Synchro files were provided to Gorove/Slade by the City and the volumes contained 
          with the existing Synchro files were confirmed by the City's signal consultant, Sabra Wang. 
     5.   All the traffic volumes appear to have been rounded, ending in either a 0 or 5.  Please explain and provide the raw 
          count data in the appendix.  The Synchro files were provided to Gorove/Slade by the City and the volumes 
          contained with the existing Synchro files were confirmed by the City's signal consultant, Sabra Wang. 
     6.   The volume directional distribution is questionable.  For example, the AM SBR at Pleasant Valley/Jubal Early is 100, 
          while the PM EBL is 450.  This type of discrepancy can be found at many locations in the model(s).  Please explain.  
          The incorrect files for the AM Synchro were provided to Gorove/Slade.  The analysis was revised using the 
          correct Synchro files. 

Gorove/Slade                                                                                                 www.goroveslade.com 
 
Millwood Avenue Traffic Diversion Study ­ Response to Comments                                                                Page 5  
March 28, 2011 
                
     7.    The existing cycle length along Pleasant Valley Rd is 180 seconds.  We understand that the consultant simply used 
           the cycle lengths provided in the Synchro model they were provided.  Certainly a 180 second cycle length is high, in 
           fact, we are not aware of a 180 second cycle length in use anywhere in the Staunton District.  That said, we field 
           checked two Pleasant Valley Road intersections during the AM, and found both to be operating at a 150 second 
           cycle length.  Please check and revise.  The signal cycle was confirmed by the City's signal consultant, Sabra 
           Wang. 
     8.    The SBR movement at Pleasant Valley Rd/Millwood Ave. is coded as a freeflow right turn movement, but 
           Millwood Ave has only one receiving lane.  We field checked the movement and noted that it operates as a yield.  
           Analysis revised.   
     9.    The default saturation flow rates for numerous movements have been manually changed.  Please explain.  The 
           defaults were calibrated by Sabra Wang based on field observations.   
     10.   The report provides pedestrian data and crash data, but did not relate the two.  For example, how many crashes 
           were pedestrian crashes?  Were there any fatalities?  An additional detailed crash analysis was performed for the 
           immediate study area and is contained within the revised study. 
     11.   The limits of the crash data move all crashes to the intersections, even if the crash occurred midblock.  The 
           absence of midblock reporting, pedestrian data, and a causation report that describes the type of crash, road 
           condition, number of vehicles, monetary damage, etc. calls into question the reliability of the consultant's safety 
           assessment.  Please explain.  As previously mentioned, an additional detailed crash analysis was performed for 
           the immediate study area and is contained within the revised study. 
     12.   The study suggests that the recommended closure may reduce the crashes at Jubal Early/Millwood by removing a 
           conflict point.  However, there is no discussion of how (or if) the 44 crashes at the Frontage Rd/Millwood/Jubal 
           Early intersection have anything to do with the Millwood Ave leg.  Are they caused by the other three legs?  
           Without a review of crash records, we find that if would be difficult if not impossible draw a conclusion.  As 
           previously mentioned, an additional detailed crash analysis was performed for the immediate study area and is 
           contained within the revised study. 
     13.   In addition, what are the safety implications of diverting Millwood traffic to a single free flow right turn lane at 
           Jubal Early and Apple Blossom Dr?  What are the causes/types of crashes occurring at this intersection, particularly 
           the westbound movement?  Again, without a detailed crash analysis, we would be reluctant to recommend an 
           alternative.  This report states that "safety was given top priority", yet little time has been spent on assessing 
           historic data, and assessing the safety implications of diverting traffic.  As previously mentioned, an additional 
           detailed crash analysis was performed for the immediate study area and is contained within the revised study. 
     14.   Referencing page 60 of the report, it concludes that "Alternative 2a was selected because: 
                a. It improves safety by eliminating ambiguous geometries, reducing vehicular conflict points, reducing curb 
                     radii and intersection skew, and creates a signalized crossing for pedestrians. 
                b. It increase convenience by reducing vehicular delays, decreasing the time it takes for pedestrians to cross 
                     Millwood Avenue, accommodates the Green Circle Trail, and improves access to the University. 
                c. It improves appearance by creating a space for a gateway treatment in the lineofsight for drivers 
                     approaching from the east, and allows for a more intuitive wayfinding systems for the same drivers. 
                d. It is well balanced because it helps both pedestrians and vehicles, shows improvements under both 
                     existing and future traffic models, and has lower cost than several of the other alternatives." 
           We would suggest that the consultant address the following observations: 
                            i. The creation of a WBR free flow movement at Jubal Early/Apple Blossom actually increases the 
                               pedestrian crossing across Jubal Early (a much more heavily traversed facility) by +/20%. 
                               It is true that the new turn lane increases the crossing distance on the eastern leg of Jubal 
                               Early, however the preferred alternative routes the Green Circle trail and primary pedestrian 
                               routing across the western leg were the crosssection remains the same and there is not the 
                               conflict with the high volume of right turns. 
                           ii. It appears difficult at best to reach any conclusion to any alternative given the limits of the crash 
                               data reviewed.  Although it may be difficult to predict future crash rates based on 
                               implementation of any of the alternatives, it is possible to compare the urban design features 
                               of the alternatives and how they affect known influences of crash rates and severity, such as 
                               speed and weaving maneuvers.   

Gorove/Slade                                                                                                     www.goroveslade.com 
 
Millwood Avenue Traffic Diversion Study ­ Response to Comments                                                        Page 6  
March 28, 2011 
                 
                       iii. Data represented in the peak hour models suggest that very few motorists actually incorrectly 
                            travel west on Millwood only to turn left to return Jubal Early and points southwest.  It is not 
                            possible to conclude from the count data how much of this activity occurs.  This was noted by 
                            several individuals during the community stakeholder meetings. 
                       iv. It is not intuitive to the reader how one could suggest that travel time and convenience is 
                            reduced for an existing Millwood Avenue user when (under the preferred alternative) travel 
                            distance increases by over 25%.  The simulation supports a reduction in "overall" delay for the 
                            study area while it is true some movements do experience increased travel time and delay 
                            while others experience a reduction. 
     15. Lastly, we would suggest that the consultant evaluate existing conditions and what "lowhanging fruit" alternatives 
         might exist to improve pedestrian access across Millwood Avenue, and/or what minor operational improvements 
         could be deployed.  Some examples might include: 
              a. Relocate all pedestrian crossings to cross Apple Blossom Drive, and then Millwood (perhaps midblock). 
              b. The installation of hawk crosswalk technology. 
              c. Raised crosswalks 
              d. Installation of median refuge island 
              e. Turn lane improvements 
         We would also suggest that a comprehensive pedestrian/bicycle count be taken over a period of two or three days.  
         A low cost option would be to video record the crossing from a remote location.  Figure 7 of the reports notes a 
         crossing during vehicular peak hours of 21 pedestrians (2 cyclists) in the morning, and 33 pedestrians (1 cycle) in 
         the evening.  Whereas, the recommended alternative cost is $1.73 million.  We feel it important to understand the 
         true nonmotorist demand of an improved crossing at this location. 
         This level of detailed analysis is beyond the scope and budget of this study.  We would suggest that additional 
         study could include a look at nearterm solutions.  However, after a thorough review of alternatives based on 
         the guiding policy documents and based on goals defined working with stakeholders, we do not believe these 
         nearterm solutions could be a substitute for the preferred alternative selected in this study.  Existing pedestrian 
         and bicycle volumes do not take into account further growth of the University population, accommodation of the 
         Green Circle Trail and an anticipated future growth in walking and biking as a mode choice.
